### Post by John.Michael.Kane on 2007-11-01
November 2007 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

---

### Post by Mazza558 on 2007-11-01
For November on my desktop PC, I've gone with a more functional "widgety" style to the desktop. This means I can get to stuff easier than in normal Gnome, but have absolutely minimal clutter. On the plus side, I can add extra "minibars" as I call them, if I want extra functionality. I can also make these completely invisible until I want them, unlike plain gnome. In terms of opening windows, I knew that although a menu you click is very nice, a keystroke launcher is just more efficient. I therefore use google desktop most of the time to run apps. "ter" gives me the terminal, "op" gives me opera, etc. I still use the normal menu from time to time, especially with the places menu.

Here is my clean desktop. The idea here is to have a "dreamy" wallpaper, which just cheers me up in general.

[[IMG]http://img212.imageshack.us/img212/4408/desk1tc8.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img212.imageshack.us/my.php?image=desk1tc8.jpg)

With lots of programs on one desktop, nothing changes to the interface. When browing the web with a maximised browser, the menus are almost invisible until you need them. "What about all your apps?" I hear you cry. Well, moving my mouse to the bottom screen runs the Scale plugin of Compiz, where the animation is sped up. This gived me a better idea of what programs I have open, and is great for cross-referencing info from a webpage onto Abiword, etc. On top of this, it gets rid of a minor annoyance of me, when people message me on Pidgin. If I'm working, a quick flick of the mouse and I can see if what they've said is worth replying to. I also turned off "show desktop when clicking background" so that it's impossible to lose my windows.

I decided to go with clearlooks due to its speed and general unified interface, with nothing I really don't like about it. In terms of Window Borders, I wasn't happy with Clearlooks particularly, so went with a simple white border.

[[IMG]http://img61.imageshack.us/img61/1327/desky2ob1.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img61.imageshack.us/my.php?image=desky2ob1.jpg)

Finally, I use the cube plugin to clear my head and if I want seperate apps on different sides of the cube. Either way scale shows all my apps running on all workspaces, giving me an overview and letting me see the big picture.

[[IMG]http://img61.imageshack.us/img61/1549/desky3eb9.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img61.imageshack.us/my.php?image=desky3eb9.jpg)

Finally, I use Xfce because of the better transparency options, simpler filemanager, and I got more stuff done while using it (at least with this interface). Also, gnome seems to have a problem with the scale plugin, in that it is very jittery, and ends up giving me a headache. With Xfce, it seems to run smoothly, at the max my monitor supports (75hz).

To summarise, these are my theme details:

Themes: Clearlooks (preinstalled) running Xfce.

Wallpaper: Can't remember the name, but it's on the 4th or 5th page of wallpapers on gnome-look.com, if you sort by best rated wallpapers.

Icons: NuoveXT 2 - I honestly haven't found a better general-purpose icon set.

Programs: Nothing really to talk about here, but the music player is Banshee (in the repos) and the filemanager is Thunar, which is on by default in Xfce.

### Post by alwiap on 2007-11-01
Well, I used to have a fascination with emulating other desktop environments and mixing them, but now I'm sticking to creating a uniquer look for gnome.  (I don't think uniquer is a word.)

also, i used to use AWM, and still have it on my box, but I really had given it some thought and I actually enjoy using the computer more without a dock and just having a panel up above to store the windows.  I find the dock to be a little monotonous, and I always would put it on auto-hide anyway since I like to have as little obstructions as possible when using applications.

i'm using a darker theme now that it's november :( , thought it would fit the weather better.  screenshots attached. 

details:

Font: Dingbats (just discovered this yesterday and loving it)
Emerald theme: QuickBlackMac (edited a bit, with Dingbats font etc.)
Background: got it from art.gnome.org i think, i honestly forget.
X11 mouse theme: Grounation (from gnome-look.org)

### Post by klange on 2007-11-01
Just got this all set up at the end of October, so it'll probably stay as is for a few more weeks:
[url=http://images.ogunderground.com/index.php?spgmGal=Halo_3][img]http://images.ogunderground.com/gal/Halo_3/_thb_cube_full.png[/img]
[img]http://images.ogunderground.com/gal/Halo_3/_thb_cube_full_b.png[/img]
[/url]
Got as many C-F plugins working as I possibly could. Getting Nautilus to have a transparent parent background was pretty easy (though the patch didn't take effect until after I had ended Nautilus, restarted it, fiddled with the preferences and then restarted my computer twice)
Emerald theme is Clean Black, but with blue. I have to admit that the title bar font is Segoe Print, I've been too lazy to change it to an open handwritten font.
Cube cap is just a random wallpaper I picked up somewhere while I was searching for wallpapers to use.
AWN is on the standard 3d theme, but with blue/clear colors.
Screenlets are the default clock and CPU, with Sidebar and ClearWeather.
GTK theme is the newer ClearLooks.
Two of the pics from Halo 3 are mine (the blue ones)
FF theme is Gnome, but it doesn't really work too well, unfortunately.
And I think that's about it...

### Post by LaRoza on 2007-11-01
There is no point in posting a screen shot, my screen is pure black, no icons, panels, bars, or anything.

I use Fluxbox, and wrote this theme:

```

#############################################################################################
#                                     Title:black+white
#                                     Written By: LaRoza
#                                     Written On: 2007
#                                     Contact: LaRozaProgramming@hotmail.com
#############################################################################################
#COMMENTS:
#           This theme is meant to be simple. It is a result of being distracted by icons, 
#               menus, buttons, and other non-essential visual elements while programming.
#           The colours are: #000000 and #FFFFFF
#############################################################################################

style.name:	black+white
style.author: LaRoza <LarozaProgramming@hotmail.com>
style.date:	2007
style.credits: LaRoza <LaRozaProgramming@hotmail.com>
style.comments: Simplistic, and does not distract.

toolbar:                             Flat 
toolbar.color:                       #000000

toolbar.button.pressed:              Flat
toolbar.button.pressed.color:        #000000

toolbar.clock:                       Flat
toolbar.clock.color:                 #000000
toolbar.clock.textColor:             #FFFFFF

toolbar.label:                       Flat
toolbar.label.color:                 #FFFFFF
toolbar.label.textColor:             #000000

toolbar.windowLabel:                 Flat
toolbar.windowLabel.color:           #FFFFFF
toolbar.windowLabel.textColor:       #000000

toolbar.justify:                     Center



menu.title:                          Flat
menu.title.color:                    #000000
menu.title.textColor:                #FFFFFF
menu.title.justify:                  Center

menu.frame:                          Flat
menu.frame.color:                    #000000

menu.frame.textColor:                #FFFFFF
menu.frame.justify:                  Left

menu.hilite:                         Flat
menu.hilite.color:                   #FFFFFF


menu.hilite.textColor:               #000000

menu.bullet:                         Diamond
menu.bullet.position:                Left



window.title.focus:                  Flat
window.title.focus.color:            #000000

window.title.unfocus:                Sunken
window.title.unfocus.color:          #000000


window.label.focus:                  Flat
window.label.focus.color:            #000000
window.label.focus.textColor:        #FFFFFF

window.label.unfocus:                Flat
window.label.unfocus.color:          #000000
window.label.unfocus.textColor:      #000000


window.button.focus:                 Flat
window.button.focus.color:           #000000
window.button.focus.picColor:        #FFFFFF

window.button.unfocus:               Flat
window.button.unfocus.color:         #000000
window.button.unfocus.picColor:      #FFFFFF

window.button.pressed:               Flat
window.button.pressed.color:         #000000


window.frame.focus:                  Sunken
window.frame.focus.color:            #888888

window.frame.unfocus:                Sunken
window.frame.unfocus.color:          #888888

window.handle.focus:                 Flat
window.handle.focus.color:           #888888

window.handle.unfocus:               Flat
window.handle.unfocus.color:         #888888


window.grip.focus:                   Flat
window.grip.focus.color:             #FFFFFF

window.grip.unfocus:                 Flat
window.grip.unfocus.color:           #888888



window.tab.justify:                  Right
window.tab.label.unfocus:            Flat
window.tab.label.unfocus.color:      #888888

window.tab.label.unfocus.textColor:  #000000
window.tab.label.focus:              Flat
window.tab.label.focus.color:        #FFFFFF

window.tab.label.focus.textColor:    black
window.tab.borderWidth:              1
window.tab.borderColor:              #000000

window.tab.font:                     snap

window.justify:                      Center

toolbar.font:                        snap
window.font:                         snap
menu.title.font:                     -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
menu.frame.font:                     -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*

#toolbar.font:                       -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#window.font:                        -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#menu.title.font:                    -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#menu.frame.font:                    -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*

borderColor:                         #FFFFFF

bevelWidth:                          2
borderWidth:                         2
handleWidth:                         3

background: Flat 
background.color: #000000


```

### Post by klange on 2007-11-01
> **alwiap said:**
> do you have a different background for each face of the cube? if so how'd you do that? i thought you couldn't do that in compiz
There's been a Wallpaper plugin for a while, which is great and all if you don't need icons. The trick is to patch Nautilus and libeel to recognize the _COMPIZ_WALLPAPER_SUPPORTED hint.
The patch is [here](http://bugzilla.gnome.org/show_bug.cgi?id=444320). You'll need the best Nautilus source you can find. I just went and picked up a 2.2.
There is one downside I and a few others have noticed: the extract shortcut normally found on the right click menu for archives is missing. I never really use it anyway as I extract most of my tarbells, etc. from Archive Manager.

Anyway, the patch will make Nautilus use a transparent background on the desktop when the Wallpaper plugin for Compiz is enabled, so it still displays the icons.

---

### Post by Caffeine_Junky on 2007-11-01
> **LaRoza said:**
> There is no point in posting a screen shot, my screen is pure black, no icons, panels, bars, or anything.

I use Fluxbox, and wrote this theme:

```

#############################################################################################
#                                     Title:black+white
#                                     Written By: LaRoza
#                                     Written On: 2007
#                                     Contact: LaRozaProgramming@hotmail.com
#############################################################################################
#COMMENTS:
#           This theme is meant to be simple. It is a result of being distracted by icons, 
#               menus, buttons, and other non-essential visual elements while programming.
#           The colours are: #000000 and #FFFFFF
#############################################################################################

style.name:	black+white
style.author: LaRoza <LarozaProgramming@hotmail.com>
style.date:	2007
style.credits: LaRoza <LaRozaProgramming@hotmail.com>
style.comments: Simplistic, and does not distract.

toolbar:                             Flat 
toolbar.color:                       #000000

toolbar.button.pressed:              Flat
toolbar.button.pressed.color:        #000000

toolbar.clock:                       Flat
toolbar.clock.color:                 #000000
toolbar.clock.textColor:             #FFFFFF

toolbar.label:                       Flat
toolbar.label.color:                 #FFFFFF
toolbar.label.textColor:             #000000

toolbar.windowLabel:                 Flat
toolbar.windowLabel.color:           #FFFFFF
toolbar.windowLabel.textColor:       #000000

toolbar.justify:                     Center



menu.title:                          Flat
menu.title.color:                    #000000
menu.title.textColor:                #FFFFFF
menu.title.justify:                  Center

menu.frame:                          Flat
menu.frame.color:                    #000000

menu.frame.textColor:                #FFFFFF
menu.frame.justify:                  Left

menu.hilite:                         Flat
menu.hilite.color:                   #FFFFFF


menu.hilite.textColor:               #000000

menu.bullet:                         Diamond
menu.bullet.position:                Left



window.title.focus:                  Flat
window.title.focus.color:            #000000

window.title.unfocus:                Sunken
window.title.unfocus.color:          #000000


window.label.focus:                  Flat
window.label.focus.color:            #000000
window.label.focus.textColor:        #FFFFFF

window.label.unfocus:                Flat
window.label.unfocus.color:          #000000
window.label.unfocus.textColor:      #000000


window.button.focus:                 Flat
window.button.focus.color:           #000000
window.button.focus.picColor:        #FFFFFF

window.button.unfocus:               Flat
window.button.unfocus.color:         #000000
window.button.unfocus.picColor:      #FFFFFF

window.button.pressed:               Flat
window.button.pressed.color:         #000000


window.frame.focus:                  Sunken
window.frame.focus.color:            #888888

window.frame.unfocus:                Sunken
window.frame.unfocus.color:          #888888

window.handle.focus:                 Flat
window.handle.focus.color:           #888888

window.handle.unfocus:               Flat
window.handle.unfocus.color:         #888888


window.grip.focus:                   Flat
window.grip.focus.color:             #FFFFFF

window.grip.unfocus:                 Flat
window.grip.unfocus.color:           #888888



window.tab.justify:                  Right
window.tab.label.unfocus:            Flat
window.tab.label.unfocus.color:      #888888

window.tab.label.unfocus.textColor:  #000000
window.tab.label.focus:              Flat
window.tab.label.focus.color:        #FFFFFF

window.tab.label.focus.textColor:    black
window.tab.borderWidth:              1
window.tab.borderColor:              #000000

window.tab.font:                     snap

window.justify:                      Center

toolbar.font:                        snap
window.font:                         snap
menu.title.font:                     -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
menu.frame.font:                     -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*

#toolbar.font:                       -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#window.font:                        -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#menu.title.font:                    -*-lucida-bold-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*
#menu.frame.font:                    -*-lucida-medium-r-*-*-*-100-*-*-*-*-*-*

borderColor:                         #FFFFFF

bevelWidth:                          2
borderWidth:                         2
handleWidth:                         3

background: Flat 
background.color: #000000


```

@ LaRoza
This is a nice Fluxbox style! ...i never thought something so simple would be so appealing!  ...thanks for shareing

### Post by klange on 2007-11-01
I put these into the info.sh bash script to grab information from Emerald and Compiz:
```
echo "* Titlebar Font:      		`grep titlebar_font= /home/[user]/.emerald/theme/theme.ini |cut -c 15-`"
echo "* Emerald Theme:		`grep description /home/[user]/.emerald/theme/theme.ini |cut -c 13-`"
echo "* Wallpapers:" # Modified for Compiz because we have more than one.
echo "`gconftool-2 --get /apps/compiz/plugins/wallpaper/screen0/options/images |cut -d "," -f 1 |sed "s/file://" |sed "s/\[//" |sed "s/:100//"`"
echo "`gconftool-2 --get /apps/compiz/plugins/wallpaper/screen0/options/images |cut -d "," -f 2 |sed "s/file://" |sed "s/:100//"`"
echo "`gconftool-2 --get /apps/compiz/plugins/wallpaper/screen0/options/images |cut -d "," -f 3 |sed "s/file://" |sed "s/:100//"`"
echo "`gconftool-2 --get /apps/compiz/plugins/wallpaper/screen0/options/images |cut -d "," -f 4 |sed "s/file://" |sed "s/\]//" |sed "s/:100//"`"
echo "* Compiz Plugins:"
echo "`gconftool-2 --get /apps/compiz/general/allscreens/options/active_plugins | sed "s/,/ /g" |sed "s/\[//" |sed "s/\]//"`"
```
The results:
[[img]http://images.ogunderground.com/gal/Halo_3/_thb_terminal.png[/img]](http://images.ogunderground.com/gal/Halo_3/terminal.png)

### Post by bunker on 2007-11-01
Boredom = re-theme KDE.  More boredom = post it on a forum.  It's Debian, but that sort of counts, right? ^^

The background is from [http://gentoo-wiki.com/TIP_GIMP_Fractal_Backgrounds](http://gentoo-wiki.com/TIP_GIMP_Fractal_Backgrounds) but it has a black tint applied to it with kdesktop.  Kicker has everything set for transparent but has a lighter blue tint applied to it.  The shell in the background is a transparent Eterm with fixed geometry and all the decorations removed, and the widget style is QtCurve for GTK and QT.  And of course conky on the right.

[[img]http://img213.imageshack.us/img213/9845/tmp4wp7.th.png[/img]](http://img213.imageshack.us/my.php?image=tmp4wp7.png)

Hm I wonder if I can fit some more terminals in there...

### Post by meindian523 on 2007-11-02
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> There's been a Wallpaper plugin for a while, which is great and all if you don't need icons. The trick is to patch Nautilus and libeel to recognize the _COMPIZ_WALLPAPER_SUPPORTED hint.
The patch is [here](http://bugzilla.gnome.org/show_bug.cgi?id=444320). You'll need the best Nautilus source you can find. I just went and picked up a 2.2.
There is one downside I and a few others have noticed: the extract shortcut normally found on the right click menu for archives is missing. I never really use it anyway as I extract most of my tarbells, etc. from Archive Manager.

Anyway, the patch will make Nautilus use a transparent background on the desktop when the Wallpaper plugin for Compiz is enabled, so it still displays the icons.

Help a noob.Please tell me how am I supposed to patch Nautilus and where do I get the sources?From the sources repo?

easwarh@l1nuxr0cks:~$ nautilus --version
GNOME nautilus 2.18.1
easwarh@l1nuxr0cks:~$

### Post by Iceni on 2007-11-02
There is a long boring story here: My gf bought a laptop about 5 years ago. It has a good cpu - xp mobile 1500. It has 256 mb ram, and one of those horribly slow hard drives they put in laptops. Then they bundled it with XP, somehow figuring this was an excellent idea...

So she left it for useless about a year or so later, and me being a bit bored a few days ago set about making it worthy. Bye bye windows, welcome ubuntu. I figured openbox should be good, and I'm loving it. It's fantastic in every way, and this old laptop is now as snappy as my dual-core desktop computer.

Thanks Fuscia for the millions of openbox screenshots and inspiration:)

Ob: Black & White 
GTK: Zenlife
Font: Kroeger

### Post by Salpiche on 2007-11-04
Emerald: vista_q
Wallpaper: DeFru
AWN: Art of Cappuccino
Conky ```

background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Monospace:size=9
xftalpha 0.8
out_to_console no
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 5
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
stippled_borders 0
border_margin 1
border_width 0
default_color white
default_shade_color white
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 2
gap_y 30
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
use_spacer no

TEXT

${color white}CPU Usage:${color red} $cpu% ${color white} 
${color white}RAM Usage:${color blue}$mem/$memmax - $memperc% 
${color white}Swap Usage:${color blue}$swap/$swapmax - $swapperc% $color 


```

everything else is in the terminal...

### Post by shearn89 on 2007-11-04
@High Camp: i've tried something similar before, and no, i don't think conky does. You'd have to write a script externally, say, if "ifconfig wlan0 = 0.0.0.0, then echo $ip_wlan0". Or something similar.

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-11-07
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Is there any possibility you could upload the tweaked window theme?... I've been in KDE several times and then came back to other GTK-based window managers, because the defaults generally suck. And I think I will have to bathe myself in howto's in order to ever understand how can someone tweak KDE into something that beautiful.

The window theme has hardly been tweaked. I just used the inbuilt configuration tools in emerald to add a few pixels to the left of the window title, and align a couple things. Really minor adjustments, things that take 2 seconds in the Emerald Settings manager. I really highly recommend the Lucidia family of fonts. I'm not a huge fan of Apple's interfaces, but they sure got fonts and icons right.

[ATTACH]49415[/ATTACH]

Anyway, My KDE theme is not that elaborate. Use apt-get to install the Domino theme engine and you're halfway there. Install the Crystal Project icons, get a nice wallpaper, and you're pretty much set. 

KDE isn't THAT hard to deal with. It's just very different from Gnome, the same way Linux in general is different when you first move over from Windows. It's worth giving a shot. I've only been using KDE for a bit more than a month, and I had it looking pretty damn nice (imho) after the first few days.

---

### Post by bonzodog on 2007-11-07
[[img]http://xs221.xs.to/xs221/07453/openzen21.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs221&d=07453&f=openzen21.png)

A simple, clean, openbox on Zenwalk Linux. Mainly for showing off the black forums :D

Also, I have done away with the title bar of the windows, which is surprisingly easy in Openbox.  All I did was went to appearances, then removed the button order, which removes the buttons altogether, and reduced the font size to 1. That reduces the title bar as far as possible. Get a theme with a title bar that matches the gtk theme colour wise, and the remaining 2 pixel title bar becomes invisible.

Used an FF extension to reduce the amount of space taken up by the icon bar area combined with the mini-fox theme.

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-11-07
> **alwiap said:**
> your attachment is amazing! I love that theme, I have one request if you are able to, could you move the minimize, maximize, and close buttons to the left side of the tab and the title in the middle?  you would be my e-hero if you could show me how to do that or do it yourself.


When you open the Emerald Theme Manager, click the "Edit Theme" tab after you've selected the theme. Then click the "Titlebar" tab, and select the OSX Layout from the drop-down menu on the right.

It's worth exploring the Emerald options, there's a lot of useful stuff in there.

EDIT: I should also mention that this is NOT my theme, it's a theme I got from kde-look.org called Azurite-Darkmod. The attachment is that theme with a couple of VERY MINOR modifications.

>  <application class="*">

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2007-11-07
> **urukrama said:**
> What is the calendar application? Looks interesting.

It is a very difficult bit of shell scripting that I wrote...  ;)
```
/home/daffy/bin $ cat calendar-display 
#!/usr/bin/env bash

cal -3 | xmessage -fg black -bg gray75 -default okay -geometry -0-30 -fn "-xos4-terminus-bold-r-normal-*-*-160-*-*-*-*-iso10646-1" -title "Three Month Calendar" -file - &

```

---

### Post by alwiap on 2007-11-07
> **sunexplodes said:**
> When you open the Emerald Theme Manager, click the "Edit Theme" tab after you've selected the theme. Then click the "Titlebar" tab, and select the OSX Layout from the drop-down menu on the right.

It's worth exploring the Emerald options, there's a lot of useful stuff in there.

EDIT: I should also mention that this is NOT my theme, it's a theme I got from kde-look.org called Azurite-Darkmod. The attachment is that theme with a couple of VERY MINOR modifications.

you're my e-hero now.  I didn't know it was that easy!

### Post by What is in a name? on 2007-11-08
So... If I had to give you all an advice, it would be...

"Use sunscreen".

Yesterday I installed the KDE-Core package, tried to do something with it for an hour and then wound up instaling the whole Kubuntu-Desktop metapackage, only to find out that the GUI wouldn't run any faster than a snail in my ATI fglrx drivers with an XGL server until I started Compiz Fusion with my KDE session (so I had to come back to Xfce to crate a .desktop file for Compiz to go in the KDE Autostart folder). Fortunately enough I put up a MySQL database to go with Amarok. Meanwhile my PC crashed sometimes with my KDE session on, and when I came back Amarok would take 2 minutes to startup, when it started up at all. Then again, Emerald would disappear without notice and never come back no matter how many times I typed "emerald --replace" in a konsole, oops, in a console. Then I tried to manage without any window borders and edit my Domino and colour scheme files to have a second alternative with warmer colours, based on the files that SunExplodes so generously uploaded to the forum (and I thank him for that). Maybe the problem was the time. It was already 3 AM and I haven't had any sleep yet, and no functional KDE session.

So, after it crashed once again, I gave up and came back to my Xfce session, leaving all the KDE cleaning process to my dear Aptitude. What a relief. No xfce4-panel, not even when I typed it in a console. Then I made a copy of my "xfce" folder under ".config" in my home folder, erased the original, logged out and logged in, and then copied my settings again. All up and running again. Today my Thunar started crashing with my Trash applet in the panel. Totally new. I'm frustrated. Maybe I'm just a depressed gay man with no patience nor mental energy to spend a whole night trying to convince a computer to work. Let's hope my awesome Xfce does not go wild too. I did keep the Emerald Azurite Darkmode theme, anyway. I don't know, what do I know about this stuff?

But trust me on the sunscreen.

---

### Post by MicroChris on 2007-11-08
> **alwiap said:**
> can you post your .conkyrc config?  I have a very simillar one (probably derived from the same) but I like some things in yours!  very nice desktop.

Thanks. Here's the conkyrc. I literally JUST removed the bit at the top that said Ubuntu 7.10, with the uptime in and the time/date. I found a Gdesklet clock I really liked, but I should've backed it up. I can probably replicate it. *EDIT* -- FIXED and edited back to original state.

```
background yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
out_to_console no
use_xft yes
xftfont Tahoma:size=7
xftalpha 0.8
mail_spool $MAIL
update_interval 1
own_window yes
#own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 120 2
maximum_width 120 2
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 1
border_width 1
#alignment top_left
gap_x 5
gap_y 5
alignment bottom_left
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes
uppercase no

TEXT

Ubuntu 7.10 ${alignr}${color #b1b1b1}($color$uptime${color #b1b1b1})$color

${color #98c2c7}TIME:$color ${alignr}${time %I:%M %p}
${color #98c2c7}DATE:$color ${alignr}${time %a %b %e %G}
${color #b1b1b1}PROCESSING ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}CPU:$color     ${alignr}${cpu cpu1}%
${color #98c2c7}${cpugraph 20,120 98c2c7}
${color #b1b1b1}DATA ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}RAM:$color       ${alignr}$memperc%
${color #98c2c7}SWAP:$color     ${alignr}$swapperc%
${color #b1b1b1}FILESYSTEM ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Root:$color ${alignr}${fs_used_perc /}%
${color #98c2c7}Data:$color       ${alignr}${fs_used_perc /media/data}%
${color #b1b1b1}NETWORK ${hr 2}$color
${color #98c2c7}Upload:$color     ${alignr}${upspeed eth0}kb/s${color #98c2c7}
${color #98c2c7}Download:$color ${alignr}${downspeed eth0}kb/s${color #98c2c7}
${color #98c2c7}Gmail:$color ${alignr}${texeci 90 python /home/chris/.gmail.py}${color #98c2c7}
```

And the gmail python script:

```
import os
import string

#Enter your username and password below within double quotes
# eg. username="username" and password="password"
username="user"
password="pass"

ttext=""
title=""
ntext=[]
nam=[]
mtext=[]
mes=[]
sum=[]
ema=[]
nom=""
tot=0
rtot=0
com="wget -O - https://"+username+":"+password+"@mail.google.com/mail/feed/atom --no-check-certificate"
      
temp=os.popen(com)
msg=temp.read()
index = string.find(msg,"<title>")
index2=string.find(msg,"</title>")  
title=msg[index+25:index2]
index=index2
index=string.find(msg,"<fullcount>")
index2=string.find(msg,"</fullcount>")
fc=msg[index+11:index2]
if(int(fc)>20):tot=20
else: tot=(int(fc))
rtot=tot

if (int(fc)==1):
   print ""+fc+" New"
elif rtot==0:
   print "0 New"
elif rtot>1:
   print ""+fc+" New"
else:
   print "Error..."

```

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-11-09
> **RobotoWorks said:**
> What are desklets?
Gdesklets are widgets/gadgets whatever you want to call them. Things such as the clock, calender, weather, etc.

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2007-11-09
desklets are similar, but I don't believe they have Vista-like clocks for it.
Gdesklets is kind of old now, but you can always look into it.
Screenlets are basically just new desklets that are designed to play nice with compiz.

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2007-11-09
Which one?

```
sudo apt-get install gdesklets gdesklets-data
```

For anything else, please find the threads about them and read those. They'll answer a lot of your questions. :)

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-11-10
> **luckyd said:**
> I have to agree, that is beautiful. Ive got Arch on a cd, and im serious thinking about installing.

This is a 10 page installation guide with screenshots of everything that you will need to do to install: [http://www.raiden.net/?cat=&aid=276](http://www.raiden.net/?cat=&aid=276)


At first the guide and the install seem a little complicated and scary, but it's worth it. Everything else after the install has nice wiki pages in the Arch forum... like:

Wireless: [http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Wireless](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Wireless)
Compiz Fusion: [http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Compiz_Fusion](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Compiz_Fusion)
Wicd: [http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Wicd](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Wicd)
Java, Adobe Reader, Flash: [http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Flash_and_Adobe_Acrobat_browser_plugins](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Flash_and_Adobe_Acrobat_browser_plugins)

### Post by jayde6 on 2007-11-10
To IIIV:

Thanks : ), weather is screenlets available at gnome-look;
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Updated+old+3rd+party+Screenlets+part1?content=64806](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Updated+old+3rd+party+Screenlets+part1?content=64806)

It is the Widescape Weather one.

clock is conky
```
#avoid flicker

double_buffer yes



#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys

own_window yes

own_window_transparent yes

own_window_type normal

own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below 



#borders

draw_borders no

border_margin 1



#shades

draw_shades no


#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
alignment top_right



#behaviour

update_interval 1



#colour
default_color ffffff


#font

use_xft yes
xftfont FreeSans:pixelsize=34

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.5


#to prevent window from moving

use_spacer no
minimum_size 0 0



TEXT
${font FreeSans:pixelsize=14}   ${time %a, %b %e}
${font}${time %l:%M}${font FreeSans:pixelsize=20}${time %p   } 
```

### Post by arbulus on 2007-11-11
> **jayde6 said:**
> To IIIV:

Thanks : ), weather is screenlets available at gnome-look;
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Updated+old+3rd+party+Screenlets+part1?content=64806](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Updated+old+3rd+party+Screenlets+part1?content=64806)

It is the Widescape Weather one.

clock is conky
```
#avoid flicker

double_buffer yes



#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys

own_window yes

own_window_transparent yes

own_window_type normal

own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below 



#borders

draw_borders no

border_margin 1



#shades

draw_shades no


#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
alignment top_right



#behaviour

update_interval 1



#colour
default_color ffffff


#font

use_xft yes
xftfont FreeSans:pixelsize=34

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.5


#to prevent window from moving

use_spacer no
minimum_size 0 0



TEXT
${font FreeSans:pixelsize=14}   ${time %a, %b %e}
${font}${time %l:%M}${font FreeSans:pixelsize=20}${time %p   } 
```



Thank you!  Your conky just made my day. I've been needing a good clock for my Openbox setup since I don't use any panels.

### Post by kshane on 2007-11-11
Everything I'm running software-wise is from the Ubuntu repositories and (mostly) installed using Synaptic.  I'm running Compiz and using the Emerald Theme Manager with Transcendental theme used to provide the bluish halo you see.

Also, I'm running the ATI Radeon X1650 graphics card with the proprietary driver installed and using AIGLX, rather than XGL.  It drags my system just a little, but looks good enough to keep it set up as you see.

I can't remember where I got the background images I used, but they're all free for private use type stuff I downloaded off the net.

The dock at the bottom is Kiba-dock.  Had a few problems installing initially, but if you use the Kiba-settings app and go slowly, it does the job!  I'm happy with it.

I waited (somewhat) patiently for ATI to release their graphic driver and it finally paid off.  Now, if they would release a more stable version than 8.42.3, I would be in heaven!

As an aside, I can run 3d games and don't have to shut down Compiz.  Everything works pretty good!

Kevin

---

### Post by ~LoKe on 2007-11-12
In the "Window Decoration" category of CCSM, look for the field that says "Decoration windows" and in that box type: !title=Terminal

Now, open up your terminal, go into the terminal, right click -> edit current profile.  "Title and Command" tab, change the initial title to "Terminal" and set "Dynamically-set title" to **Isn't displayed**.

---

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-11-13
> **mysticrider92 said:**
> How did you get the terminal to show no window borders? Or is that your compiz theme? I really like that look.

Hello, sorry for the late reply. To get the embedded terminal I followed this guide that shows how to do it with the Compiz Fusion ccsm: [http://ubuntology.com/2007/10/25/howto-embedded-terminal-on-your-gutsy-desktop/](http://ubuntology.com/2007/10/25/howto-embedded-terminal-on-your-gutsy-desktop/)

It is an individual terminal that you can turn on and off. It uses a profile that you make in your Gnome Terminal called embedded, then using Compiz Fusion's advanced settings of Window Management-->--Window Rules, and Window Management-->-- Place Windows-->--Fixed Window Placement, it allows it to be placed on your desktop without the window borders or menu bar.

### Post by crimesaucer on 2007-11-14
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Pretty much the same setup I had before. Except that now I get to see the Coliseum of Rome every day. I find it refreshing. Others find it decadent.

But hey, at least I am listening to one of my favourite bands.
Nightwish 4ever.

[[IMG]http://img204.imageshack.us/img204/6797/ecra1ps7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img204.imageshack.us/my.php?image=ecra1ps7.jpg)[[IMG]http://img267.imageshack.us/img267/672/ecra2pi1.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img267.imageshack.us/my.php?image=ecra2pi1.jpg)[[IMG]http://img46.imageshack.us/img46/1641/ecra3pe1.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img46.imageshack.us/my.php?image=ecra3pe1.jpg)

P.S.: I so have to decide what to do with that Xfce-panel. I want it to be there, but it always looks unattractive no matter where I put it.

What you might want to do is to make a .gtkrc-2.0 with a panel image that you can make transparent by about 20%...

Try to make it match the color of your window borders. On xfce4, the icons will also become a bit transparent, but at 20% it's not that bad and your font (#FFFFFF) will still be very readable.

This is my .gtkrc-2.0 for my panel, I just put it into my /home/folder:

```

style "panel"
{
  bg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
  bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = "panel-73.png"
  fg[NORMAL] = "#FFFFFF"
  }

widget_class "*Panel*"      style "panel"
widget "*Panel*"            style "panel"
class "*Panel*"             style "panel"

```

..."panel-73.png" is an image I use that matches my Emerald widow theme.

... "#000000" is for the background color of separators and for the line on the top of the panel... it will also be the border around the xfce4 volume plug-in, but I use the gnome volume plug-in because it is better looking than the xfce4 one (no ugly green, and no border).

... "#FFFFFF" is for your panel font color.

Here is an example of my xfce4 panel:

[IMG]http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-75b-2.png[/IMG]
1200 x800 view: [http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-75b.png](http://i144.photobucket.com/albums/r161/crimesaucer/Screenshot-75b.png)

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-14
> **el mariachi said:**
> mine for this month, still a work in progress
I have a new theme in the oven ;)

Nice, mariachi. What's on the wallpaper?

Here is my current Openbox setup. The wallpaper is based on a picture of refugee children in a Sri Lankan refugee camp (housing victims from the 2004 tsunami) taken by [archange]("http://archange.deviantart.com/art/Refugee-camp-7-41652098").

Openbox theme is the dark version of Red Giant (I really should rename that theme...); gtk theme is a modification of Rezlooks L&D; icons are Minimal Perception. Fonts are HeldustryFTVBasic Black (window headers), Sans (menus and gtk) and yataghan (conky). 

The setup is inspired by the anarcho-christian punkish-folk group [The Psalters]("http://www.psalters.com/"). I've been listening quite a lot to them lately :D

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2007-11-15
> **el mariachi said:**
> btw: no one  must've noticed it.. My fonts (the title bar ones) don't look smooth like before (before Gutsy). How can I enable hinting o something manually? (I'm running pure OpenBox no gnome or kde or anything)

Create a ~/.fonts.conf file and configure your desired settings there.

"man fonts-conf" for details.  Here are the settings I use with my LCD display as an example:
```
/home/daffy $ cat .fonts.conf 
<?xml version="1.0"?>

<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">

<fontconfig>
  <match target="font" >
      <edit mode="assign" name="rgba" >     <const>rgb</const>      </edit>
      <edit mode="assign" name="hinting" >  <bool>true</bool>       </edit>
      <edit mode="assign" name="antialias"> <bool>true</bool>       </edit>
      <edit mode="assign" name="autohint" > <bool>false</bool>      </edit>
      <edit mode="assign" name="hintstyle"> <const>hintfull</const> </edit>
  </match>
  <!-- Disable hinting for bold fonts -->
  <match target="font">
      <test name="weight"    compare="more"> <const>medium</const>   </test>
      <edit name="autohint"  mode="assign">  <bool>false</bool>      </edit>
      <edit name="hinting"   mode="assign">  <bool>false</bool>      </edit>
      <edit name="hintstyle" mode="assign">  <const>hintnone</const> </edit>
  </match>
</fontconfig>

```

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-16
Here is my latest Openbox theme: Prelude.

It started as a green theme (screenshot one), but I changed it to brown (second screenshot), matching my Terrene gtk theme. I've uploaded the brown version to box-look.org ([here]("http://box-look.org/content/show.php?content=69899")); perhaps the green one will follow, perhaps not.

Details: Openbox 3.4, Openbox theme is Prelude, fonts are HeldustryFTVBasic Black (window decorations), Sans (menu) and yataghan (conky). Wallpapers are homemade. Shadows are achieved with xcompmgr.

Feedback is always welcome.

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-16
> **Lord_Dicranius said:**
> So simple, yet so...I wish I had a bigger vocabulary hehe  I love these :)

> **el mariachi said:**
> wow great urukrama!
btw: what does that mean (first wallpaper)?

Thank you both. :D

The text on the first wallpaper is a mantra from the *Bhagavata*, a classic Hindu sacred text. It means "I repeatedly bow before the Lord, Dharma, who purifies the mind and self." Dharma is a name of God, and means both "he who is firmly established" as "he who maintains". Dharma is also a term that refers to the spritual and ethical path one follows. The implication is that God is not just the goal of one's spiritual practice, but is also the practice itself. It is one of my favourite mantras.

---

### Post by undine on 2007-11-16

The text on the first wallpaper is a mantra from the *Bhagavata*, a classic Hindu sacred text. It means "I repeatedly bow before the Lord, Dharma, who purifies the mind and self." Dharma is a name of God, and means both "he who is firmly established" as "he who maintains". Dharma is also a term that refers to the spritual and ethical path one follows. The implication is that God is not just the goal of one's spiritual practice, but is also the practice itself. It is one of my favourite mantras.

### Post by Vansinnesvisan on 2007-11-16
> **komensky said:**
> Awsome desk... congrats.

Could you please share your terminal profile & prompt theme?
Thanks a lot.

It's pretty much the default stuff; sans scroll bar, grey background and Bitstream font.

My .bashrc is:
```
BLUE=`tput setf 1`
GREEN=`tput setf 2`
CYAN=`tput setf 3`
RED=`tput setf 4`
MAGENTA=`tput setf 5`
YELLOW=`tput setf 6`
WHITE=`tput setf 7`
PS1='\[$MAGENTA\]\u@\h \[$BLUE\]\w/\[$GREEN\] \$\[$WHITE\] '
```

### Post by walkerk on 2007-11-17
> **IIIV said:**

Is your calendar on the upper right Conky?

Thanks.. yea its conky. Heres the command...
```
cal | awk 'NR>1' | sed -e 's/   /    /g' -e 's/[^ ] /& /g' -e 's/..*/  & /' -e 's/ \('`date | awk '{print $3}'`'\) /\['`date | awk '{print $3}'`'\]/'
```

### Post by walkerk on 2007-11-17
> **IIIV said:**
> Thanks... I'm actually a Linux newbie, so how exactly do I use that calendar code? I tried putting it in my .conkyrc file and it doesn't work... Any more info would be really appreciated.

Thanks!
this should do it...
```
${execi 300 cal | awk 'NR>1' | sed -e 's/   /    /g' -e 's/[^ ] /& /g' -e 's/..*/  & /' -e 's/ \('`date | awk '{print $3}'`'\) /\['`date | awk '{print $3}'`'\]/'}
```

### Post by markupstart on 2007-11-18
I like it, I've tried it before but never bothered to configure it to my liking.  There are lots of configuration options, there are several files you can edit to change some settings, the file themselves are well commented to make it clear what each item does.  
Just take a look at the how-to link someone posted, it is a pretty good start to configuring Icewm.  I use Rox for desktop icons and file manager.









> **shearn89 said:**
> @markupstart: nice. How do you find IceWM? easy to use/set up? Lots of customization options? I'm interested in trying new wms that are quite light.

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-18
**Shearn**, feel free to modify that theme. It is under the GPL licence, so you can do with it as you wish. 

IceWM is pretty nice. It has is highly (and easily) configurable. I quite like it, though I feel much more comfortable using Openbox (it's in the little things, you know). The one thing I really like about IceWM is that you can have a vertical alt-tab dialog. The downside is that I find it hard to find a theme that suits my tastes.

EDIT: Oh, and my xcompmgr settings are as follows:
> xcompmgr -cC -t-3 -l-5 -r5

**Oldster**: thank you.

**BrettRS**: nice one.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-19
> **shearn89 said:**
> I can if you want - not sure how to package it as an .obt

You can use Obconf for that. It has a button "create .obt archive" (under the theme previews). Select the directory where your theme's "openbox-3" folder is located and press enter (In other words, for my Prelude theme, I open the 'Prelude' folder, but not the "openbox-3" folder within that). It is as simple as that. 

It might also work if you create a tar.gz archive, and rename that to an .obt archive (it works the other way, at least).

---

### Post by epimer on 2007-11-19
I went a bit Tango this month. I tried changing the panel to something lighter, but nothing I tried looked as slick (to me) as the existing config (the background image is the KDEmod default); tried out the Crystal Project and OSK icons, but neither were as clear, functional and still as pretty as the KDEmod Tango ones. So I went for a new theme around them.

Icons: KDEmod Tango
Wallpaper: Posted by someone at the Arch forums, and I think they got it from DeviantArt
Style: Domino - config based on Edge, but tweaked a little by me.
Colours: Gilouche
Window decorations: kind_of_blue Emerald theme.

### Post by fuscia on 2007-11-19
ok, this might seem stupid (and it is), but once i realized it was ctrl+alt+Fwhatever to get into the console (and not just alt+Fsomething), i realized i have a lot less of a need for a wm. so, i put feh, opera and 9wm in my .xinitrc and just use the gui for browsing (text browsers are a nightmare, unless you're reading a book online), thunar (some file managment is just easier that way) and gimp. it's kind of neat to be switching in and out of the console and gui, kind of like being in a borges short story. anyway, here it is: 9wm, opera (redglist skin), urxvt. ### Post by epimer on 2007-11-22
Inspired by the choice of the final KDE4 wallpapers, I decided to knock up this autumnal variant.

Style, as before, is Domino with a slightly tweaked Edge config.
Emerald theme is Azurite-Darkmod-Round (thanks, sunexplodes!).
Icons are KDEmod Tango.
Colours are Concrete 32: Half Baked
Wallpaper is from the KDE4 wallpaper choices; I don't have the link to hand but it's got to be all over the Linux news sites by now!
Apps shown are Konqueror with the Baghira sidebar, and Opera with the Tango theme.

---

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-11-22
> **epimer said:**
> Inspired by the choice of the final KDE4 wallpapers, I decided to knock up this autumnal variant.

Style, as before, is Domino with a slightly tweaked Edge config.
Emerald theme is Azurite-Darkmod-Round (thanks, sunexplodes!).
Icons are KDEmod Tango.
Colours are Concrete 32: Half Baked
Wallpaper is from the KDE4 wallpaper choices; I don't have the link to hand but it's got to be all over the Linux news sites by now!
Apps shown are Konqueror with the Baghira sidebar, and Opera with the Tango theme.


That looks fantastic. Not such a big fan of the Tango iconset, but that wallpaper is beautiful, and the panel's really nicely laid out (despite being just a LITTLE too small for my tastes). And you know how I love that emerald theme. 

I just found out a little tweak you might be interested in, btw. The only Konqueror sidebar I use AT ALL is the Baghira one, and so I start to hate those tabs on the side. You can hide them by editing ~/.kde/share/config/konqsidebartng.rc and setting HideTabs to "true" under the FileManagement heading. Looks a lot nicer to me.

Anyway, keep up the good work, I love seeing not-ugly KDE desktops!

---

### Post by j.miller565 on 2007-11-22
> **shearn89 said:**
> nice. Simple.

Is the transparent panel a new Gutsy option?

It's been there in Feisty too. if you want ot use it just go into Panel Properties by right clicking the panel and then clicking on Properties. Then click on the Background Tab and you should see 3 options: None (use system theme), Solid Colour, Background Image. 

Choose Solid Colour. Clicke on the colour button to get a colour wheel. Choose what colour you want. Then press OK. If you want it to be transparent of slighty transparent, move the slider down to Transparent.

Hope this helps if you would like transparent panels. :)

---

### Post by arbulus on 2007-11-24
> **Frak said:**
> In case you want to: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu)


Even though that howto has uninstallation instructions, they don't work.  Once you've installed it, you ***cannot undo it***. All you can do is put a line in you .gtkrc file to make it not appear if you don't want it, but you cannot completely get rid of it.  I tried the whole reinstalling gtk, but it doesn't work. 

It seriously goofed up my system.  I ended up having to just reinstall Ubuntu in the end. 

It may look neat, but be careful if you use it.

---

### Post by Frak on 2007-11-24
> **arbulus said:**
> Even though that howto has uninstallation instructions, they don't work.  Once you've installed it, you ***cannot undo it***. All you can do is put a line in you .gtkrc file to make it not appear if you don't want it, but you cannot completely get rid of it.  I tried the whole reinstalling gtk, but it doesn't work. 

It seriously goofed up my system.  I ended up having to just reinstall Ubuntu in the end. 

It may look neat, but be careful if you use it.
You must comment out the apt-build localhost repository before you can restore the original libgtk. Else you'll just get md5sum errors.

### Post by dbbolton on 2007-11-24
> **nikoPSK said:**
> Like that, I'm going to grab that gtk theme.
I forgot to mention, I made a couple slight modifications in the gtkrc file.

I changed this:
```

  engine "murrine" 
  {
   scrollbar_color = "#F1EFEB" # deepsky
    contrast = 1.5
    glazestyle = 0 # 0 = flat hilight, 1 = curved hilight, 2 = concave style
    menubarstyle = 2 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = gradient, 3 = striped
    menubaritemstyle = 1 # 0 = menuitem look, 1 = button look
    menuitemstyle = 1 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = striped
    menustyle = 0
    scrollbarstyle = 3
    listviewstyle = 1
    listviewheaderstyle = 1 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy
    roundness = 1 # 0 = squared, 1 = old default, more will increase roundness
    animation = TRUE # FALSE = disabled, TRUE = enabled
       hilight_ratio = 1.0
        gradients = TRUE
   }

```

to this:
```

  engine "murrine" 
  {
   scrollbar_color = "#F1EFEB" # deepsky
    contrast = 1.5
    glazestyle = 0 # 0 = flat hilight, 1 = curved hilight, 2 = concave style
    menubarstyle = 3 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = gradient, 3 = striped
    menubaritemstyle = 1 # 0 = menuitem look, 1 = button look
    menuitemstyle = 1 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy, 2 = striped
    menustyle = 0
    scrollbarstyle = 2
    listviewstyle = 1
    listviewheaderstyle = 1 # 0 = flat, 1 = glassy
    roundness = 0 # 0 = squared, 1 = old default, more will increase roundness
    animation = TRUE # FALSE = disabled, TRUE = enabled
       hilight_ratio = 1.0
        gradients = TRUE
   }

```

### Post by arbulus on 2007-11-24
> **fuscia said:**
> xfce, glitch window dec., thunar, amora icons, nova blue gtk, urxvt and some wallpaper i've grossly distorted...


You know, I've not really given xfce a fair go in the past.  But I recently tried it out,  and I have to say I'm pretty impressed with it.  I use Openbox normally, but xfce is like a nifty blend of Openbox and Gnome. It has a lot of the things I love from Openbox, but the whole package of a full DE that's kinda Gnome-like (I prefer Gnome over KDE as DEs go.)

I think that if I were to ever go back to a full DE for everyday use, I would probably use xfce.

### Post by LinuxGuy1234 on 2007-11-25
> **SD-Plissken said:**
> November 2007 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

[IMG]http://asteinborn78.ej.am/desktop/Screenshot.png[/IMG]

Theme: Vista Basic border and Windows XP control themes at [art.gnome.org]("http://art.gnome.org/")
Wallpaper: one of the wallpapers in Ubuntu
Icons: one of the icons in Ubuntu
Programs: base Ubuntu programs

I love your wallpaper.

### Post by D-EJ915 on 2007-11-27
> **plb said:**
> Nostalgia ftw :)
[http://xs321.xs.to/xs321/07482/fvwm.jpg.xs.jpg](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs321&d=07482&f=fvwm.jpg)I agree, can't beat FVWM for customizability, plus it's extremely snappy.

You should make the iconified icons be thumbnails though, lemme grab some code to put in...then just stick "Thumbnail" in instead of iconify for your button definitions, etc.

[size=0]     DestroyFunc Thumbnail
     AddToFunc Thumbnail
     + I Raise
     + I ThisWindow (!Shaded, Iconifiable, !Iconic) PipeRead \
         "xwd -silent -id $[w.id] | convert -scale 100 -frame 1x1 \
         -mattecolor black -quality 0 xwd:- \
         png:$[FVWM_USERDIR]/icon.tmp.$[w.id].png \
         && echo WindowStyle IconOverride, \
         Icon $[FVWM_USERDIR]/icon.tmp.$[w.id].png \
         || echo Nop"
     + I Iconify

DestroyFunc DeThumbnail
     AddToFunc DeThumbnail
     + I Exec rm -f $[FVWM_USERDIR]/icon.tmp.$[w.id].png
     + I DestroyWindowStyle

     *FvwmEvent: deiconify DeThumbnail

     AddToFunc StartFunction I Module FvwmEvent[/size]

---

### Post by regeya on 2007-11-27
Inspired to switch back to Window Maker after seeing a screenshot in this thread.  :)

Toolkit theme: QtCurve
Window Maker theme:  one I'm working on :)
Background:  My l'il girl playing in the yard this spring :)

Screenshots don't do Window Maker justice, though.  It has a rather inflexible look-and-feel, and lacks that RGBA support so many people find "essential" these days.  But by golly, I'd grown so used to inflexible desktops that I'd forgotten just what a pleasure--and how easy--Window Maker is to work with.

Now if only someone would fix DND support.

### Post by billgoldberg on 2007-11-30
[[img]http://xs321.xs.to/xs321/07485/Screenshot-1.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs321&d=07485&f=Screenshot-1.png)

details from system -> preferences -> apperance

**controls:** Linista GTK2

**window border:** Moomex

**icons:** NueveXT-1.6

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**black firefox icon: ***[here]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Firefox+Icons?content=47617")*
(install the icon: sudo nautilus -> usr -> share -> pixmaps -> replace "firefox.png" with the new icon, make sure to name the new icon firefox.png)

**wallpaper:** *[here]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/darkyfox?content=67293")*

**firefox theme: ***[here]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/4988")*

**curved AWN dock: ***[guide]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=572019")*

### Post by wizard10000 on 2007-11-30
> **alwiap said:**

Change auto_hide_size from 6 to 1.

### Post by wickstopher on 2007-11-30
This is Linux Mint 4.0 Daryna KDE CE (based on Kubuntu Gutsy).  I hate icons on the desktop, so I have that disabled, and I also dislike panels and panel menus in the taskbar.  I much prefer the KDE middle-mouse-button click on the desktop to get a drop-down menu of open windows/applications.  Other than that, it's a pretty straightforward desktop without much modification.  The wallpaper is an image from an artist friend of mine, Dave Rosen ([http://www.davidabrahamrosen.com]("http://www.davidabrahamrosen.com")) using the Pyramid Blending option in the KDE desktop configuration.

[[IMG]http://www.christopherwicks.com/bucket/snapshot2scale.png[/IMG]]("http://www.christopherwicks.com/bucket/snapshot2.png")
